***cannon.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> cannon (7664)</h1><br></body> 
***cannonball.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a> (47666)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cannon</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">ball</i> from being a round ball that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> fired from a cannon.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">cannonballs</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">military<span class="ib-comma">,</span> artillery</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span>
<ol><li>A spherical projectile fired from a smoothbore cannon
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonyms:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">solid shot</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">ball</span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en">round shot</span></span></dd></dl></li>
<li>An explosive-filled hollow iron sphere fused through a hole and intended to explode at a calculated distance rather than explode on impact.</li></ol></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From behaving like a <a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a> fired from a cannon
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">cannonballs</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">diving</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The act of running and <a href = vnd.unilang:jumping.html>jumping</a> in a flexed position into a swimming pool to create a large splash, mimicking the flight and shape of a <a class="mw-selflink selflink"><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a></a>.
<dl><dd>The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a></b> could be called the S.<a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>U</a>.V. of the pool  |  oversized, brash, hormonally hardwired.
<ul><li><i>The New Yorker,</i> 30 August 2004, p.40</li></ul></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> figuratively</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Something that <a href = vnd.unilang:moves.html>moves</a> fast.
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:meetings.html>Meetings</a> of the model train club always begin with the song "Wabash <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>Cannonball</a></b>".</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">tennis</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A served ball that travels with great speed and describes little or no arc in flight.</li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">cannonballs</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cannonballing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cannonballed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To jump/dive into water doing a <a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a> landing.
<dl><dd><i>He <b>cannonballed</b> into the pool, drenching us all.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li>To careen; to move rapidly</li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a>!</strong>
</p>
<ol><li>Yelled when <a href = vnd.unilang:jumping.html>jumping</a>/diving into the water, doing a <a href = vnd.unilang:cannonball.html>cannonball</a> landing.</li></ol>
</body>

***cantaloupe.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupe.html>cantaloupe</a> (76784)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">cantaloup</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">Cantalupo</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="ann-pos">a place name</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, after a former Papal summer estate near <a href = vnd.unilang:rome.html>Rome</a>, where the melons <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> first grown after being introduced to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupe.html>cantaloupe</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupes.html>cantaloupes</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A melon of species <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Cucumis_melo_subsp._melo" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Cucumis melo subsp. melo"><i>Cucumis melo</i> subsp. <i>melo</i></a></span> with sweet orange flesh, with numerous cultivars in several cultivar groups.
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ireland" class="extiw" title="w:Ireland">Ireland</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Smooth-skinned, also known as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/true_cantaloupe" class="extiw" title="w:true cantaloupe">true <a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupe.html>cantaloupe</a></a>, found in the Middle East and also grown in Europe. <span class="defdate">[From 1739.]</span></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia" class="extiw" title="w:Australia">Australia</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Having a rough skin resembling netting; also known as muskmelon or rockmelon.</li></ol></li>
<li>An orange colour, like that of <a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupe.html>cantaloupe</a> flesh.
<dl><dd><div class="color-panel"><a href = vnd.unilang:cantaloupe.html>cantaloupe</a> colour: <span style="background-color:FFA62F; display:inline-block; width:80px;"> </span></div></dd></dl></li></ol>
</body>

***canter.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a> (108347)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Short for <i>Canterbury pace</i>, from the supposed easy pace of medieval <a href = vnd.unilang:pilgrims.html>pilgrims</a> to Canterbury.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">canters</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A gait of a horse between a trot and a gallop, consisting of three <a href = vnd.unilang:beats.html>beats</a> and a "suspension" phase, where there are no <a href = vnd.unilang:feet.html>feet</a> on the ground. Also describing this gait on other four legged animals.</li>
<li>A ride on a horse at such speed.</li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">canters</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cantering</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">cantered</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To move at such pace.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To cause to move at a <a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a>; to ride (a horse) at a <a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a>.</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">cant</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i>
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">canters</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>One who cants or whines; a beggar.</li>
<li>One who <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> hypocritical pretensions to goodness; one who uses canting language.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1849–1861</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Babington_Macaulay" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Babington Macaulay">Thomas Babington Macaulay</a>,  chapter 11, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_History_of_England_from_the_Accession_of_James_the_Second" class="extiw" title="w:The History of England from the Accession of James the Second">The History of England from the Accession of James the Second</a></cite>, volume <span class="maintenance-line" style="color: 777777;">(please specify |volume=I to V)</span>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longman" class="extiw" title="w:Longman">Longman, Brown, Green, and Longmans</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/1069526323">1069526323</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The days when he <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:canter.html>canter</a></b> and a rebel.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1974</b>,  Bill Wannan,  <cite>With Malice Aforethought</cite>, page 85:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">From lawn-sleeved ranters to kerbstone <b>canters</b>, From <a href = vnd.unilang:bishops.html>bishops</a> to Army lasses.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:cao.html>cao</a> (49819)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cao.html>cao</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cao.html>cao</a>'s</b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:cao.html>cao</a>'tje</b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zelfstandig_naamwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zelfstandig.html>Zelfstandig</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naamwoord.html>naamwoord</a></i></span></h4>

***capisce.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:capisce.html>capisce</a> (70692)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed (with a change of spelling reflecting the <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a> pronunciation) from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it"><a href = vnd.unilang:capisci.html>capisci</a></i>, the second-person singular present indicative form of <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">capire</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to understand</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, through <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">*capīre</i> from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">capere</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to grasp, seize</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Italic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Italic language">Proto-Italic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="itc-pro">*kapiō</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*kh₂pyéti</i>, from the root <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*keh₂p-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to grab, to seize</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:capisce.html>capisce</a>?</strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> “Get it?”; “understood?”.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1995</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bart_Simpson" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Bart Simpson">Bart Simpson</a>,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marge_Be_Not_Proud" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Marge Be Not Proud"><a href = vnd.unilang:marge.html>Marge</a> Be Not Proud</a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Simpsons" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd></dd></dl></div>
<dl><dd>Brodka: <a href = vnd.unilang:hey.html>Hey</a>, kid: one more thing. If you <i>ever</i> set foot in this store again, you'<a href = vnd.unilang:ll.html>ll</a> be spending Christmas in juvenile hall. <b><a href = vnd.unilang:capisce.html>Capisce</a>?</b></dd>
<dd>Bart: [silence]</dd>
<dd>Brodka: Well, do you understand?</dd>
<dd>Bart: Everything except “<b><a href = vnd.unilang:capisce.html>capisce</a>.</b>”</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1996</b>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bound_(1996_film)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Bound (1996 film)">Bound</a></cite>, written by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wachowskis" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Wachowskis">The Wachowskis</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dino_De_Laurentiis_Cinematografica" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Dino De Laurentiis Cinematografica"><a href = vnd.unilang:dino.html>Dino</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> Laurentiis Productions</a> and Spelling <a href = vnd.unilang:films.html>Films</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:gino.html>Gino</a> Marzzone: You gotta start respecting <a href = vnd.unilang:johnny.html>Johnny</a>, the way you respect <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a>. <b><a href = vnd.unilang:capisce.html>Capisce</a></b>?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1997</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Bogosian" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Eric Bogosian"><a href = vnd.unilang:eric.html>Eric</a> Bogosian</a>,  <cite>Notes from Underground</cite>, page 138:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">It's very simple, George, you forget about this whole licensing lawsuit pipe dream of yours or you can forget about your <a href = vnd.unilang:buddy.html>buddy</a> working in my factory for the next couple of years. I <i>will</i> be that angry. <i><b>Capiche?</b></i></span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2003</b>,  Richard Chiappone,  <cite>Water of an Undetermined Depth</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">I mean, if you <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> coming into the plant for the long haul, <a href = vnd.unilang:god.html>God</a> forbid, then you'd have to think seriously about the money. <b>Capiche</b>?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li>Often used in a threatening manner, in imitation of the way the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Mafia" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Italian Mafia">Italian Mafia</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> often portrayed in popular culture and entertainment media.</li>
<li>Without a question mark at the end, it <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> sometimes used to mean, “I understand”, as an American colloquialism. In Italian, that would actually mean “he/she/it understands” or a formal “you understand”. To mean “I understand”, one would actually say <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">capisco</i>.</li></ul>
</body>

<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">capitulation</i>. Equivalent to <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:capituleren.html>capituleren</a></i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">-atie</i>.

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

</p>

<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> electoral agreement stipulating conditions on the Holy Roman Emperor

***cardioloog.html

<p>Borrowed, though it <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> difficult to determine from what language. Equivalent to <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">cardio-</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">-loog</i>. First attested in the 1920s.
</p>
